ANNEX G
REPUBLIC OF TAJIKISTAN
PILOT POVERTY ALLEVIATION PROJECT
SOCIAL PROTECTION MEASURES SUPPORTED THROUGH THE AGRICULTURAL
REFORM AND SOCIAL PROTECTION PROJECT
1.    The Agricultural Reforn and Social Protection Credit supports Government's efforts to improve
social programs in three specific areas by: (a) protecting social sector bud get allocations; (b) improving
the targeting of safety net expenditures; and (c) restructuring pension and social insurance programs.
PROTECTING HEALTH AND EDUCATION EXPENDITURES
2.    Since 1992, the education and health sectors have been severely impaired by the collapse in
Government revenues and expenditures. The combined share of GDP that was allocated to these two
sectors was 17 percent in 1992 and about seven percent of a much smaller GDP in 1995. As a
consequence, supplies are scarce, wage payments have been irregular, and highly qualified staff continue
to leave both sectors. School attendance is falling and indicators show a worsening of the nation's health,
especially in the rural areas. There is an urgent need for emergency measures in these two sectors,
including immediate efforts to improve the supply of textbooks and basic drugs. In the short-term, the
priority is to ensure that these sectors receive a reasonable share of the severely constrained budget.
Consequently, Government allocated a fifth of the 1996 budget to these two sectors -- 5.5 percent to
health and 14.5 percent to education.
TARGETING SOCIAL PAYMENTS: ALLOWANCES AND SUBSIDIES
3.    Historically, household allowances and public enterprise subsidies were unsustainably large (18
percent of GDP in 1994) and inefficiently delivered. Subsidies to public enterprises, which represented
about 13 percent of GDP in 1994, were a major part of the overall social protection system in Tajikistan
because they allowed consumer prices to be kept below the cost of production. The bulk of these
subsidies were for bread production (paras. 41 and 42), irrigation (para. 30), and transportation. To
protect the poor from liberalization of transport prices, the Government will explore options for the use
of transport vouchers for selected groups.The most important element of the social safety net in Tajikistan
is the bread compensation allowance. Tajik households consume a relatively high level of bread products.
Prior to May 1995, the Government provided a universal bread allowance of 1,800 Russian rubles for
each citizen (representing 4.5 percent of GDP in 1994). Additionally, bread production was heavily
subsidized (8.4 percent of GDP in 1994). As of July 1995, these subsidies amounted to 50 percent of
the price of a loaf of bread and constituted an expensive universal subsidy that did little to target the poor.
In August 1995, both the bread compensation allowance and the production subsidy were replaced by the
reintroduction of a targeted bread allowance and a child allowance. In December 1995, the bread
compensation allowance was doubled to compensate partially for liberalized bread prices. On March 1,



- 103 -
1996, the Government fully liberalized the prices of bread and flour and increased the bread compensation
allowance by an additional 70 percent. (Between August 1995 and June 1996 bread prices rose
approximately eightfold reflecting the removal of public subsidies and higher local currency prices for
imported wheat.) At the same time, the bread compensation and child allowances were combined into
single social welfare payment. This social welfare payment, which amounts to TR500 per month, was
targeted to children under 16 years old (for households with per capita income less than twice the
minimum wage), non-working pensioners whose pensions are less than double the minimum wage,
registered unemployed workers, and the disabled. Because of the dramatic changes in the economy in
recent years, the present targeting system (which is based on 1993 household survey data) needs to be
revised. The Government has decided to undertake a household survey in order to provide a better basis
for targeting. In the 1996 budget, Government allocated TR7.8 billion for social welfare compensation.
This allocation assumes 1.4 million of beneficiaries (out of a population of 5.8 million). Should the
number of applicants for assistance during 1996 prove to be higher than expected, the Government will,
in consultation with IDA, adopt corrective measures to keep the total amount of allowances within the
budget allocation.
TARGETING SOCIAL PAYMENTS: PENSION, SOCIAL INSURANCE AND EMPLOYMENT
BENEFITS
4.    In 1991, Government set up three extra-budgetary funds to replace the large social transfers from
Moscow. Each of the three funds was given a share of the 39 percent tax on enterprise wage bills. Of
the three funds, the largest is the Pension Fund, which receives just over 32 percentage points of the tax.
The Social Insurance Fund and the Employment Fund account for six and one percentage points of the
payroll tax, respectively. Since the end of 1993, inflation and the downward spiral of output has meant
that enterprises have been unable or unwilling to pay the wage bill tax with the result that each of the
funds has suffered serious revenue shortfalls. In turn, there have been many months when the funds have
not been able to make payments to their beneficiaries. The current economic and financial situation
provides little ground for optimism that regular full payments will be resumed in the near term.
5.    The Pension Fund is responsible for the payment of retirement benefits (about three-quarters of
the Fund's obligations) as well as payments for invalids and some other social benefits. Presently, there
are numerous structural problems with the Pension Fund that have contributed to the current crisis.
These include: (a) the fund's promise to pay pensions on the basis of workers' previous income, as if
those workers were paying into an investment account, whereas current pension payments are based on
current payments by enterprises; (b) isolation from the central government budgetary process; and (c) a
rate of taxation on the wage bill is too high. Consequently, the system needs to be reformed to create
an effective and sustainable social safety net -- albeit one with lower levels of benefits than during the
Soviet era. Therefore, in June 1996, as a temporary measure, Government limited: (a) the value of
pensions in order to achieve greater regularity in payments; and (b) the monthly payment to the amount
of actual revenue collections. Further, Government has announced that all pensioners will be paid at the
minimum rate and that the monthly surplus in the Pension Fund, if any, will be distributed to the eligible
pensioners proportionately to their entitlements. Any arrears that are accumulated will be canceled at
the end of each quarter. Additionally, Government has announced that pensions will no longer be paid
to working pensioners.In order to improve the administration of social insurance, in February 1996,
Government consolidated the collection of all payroll taxes under the responsibility of a single agency and
centralized the collection and allocation of Pension Fund revenues to mitigate regional disparities. In



-104-
addition, the Government removed the responsibility for paying child allowances from the Pension Fund
and integrated it with the social welfare payment.
6.    The Social Insurance Fund is an extra-budgetary fund managed by the Governing Council of
Trade Unions that pays sick leave and maternity benefits and also provides various worker amenities.
As with the Pension Fund, the Social Insurance Fund has been unable to meet its commitments in recent
years. Entitlement are generous by international standards and give rise, when in operation, to excessive
use of limited health care services. Sick leave benefits provide up to 100 percent of a worker's salary
for up to four months and birth grants are provided for up to three children. Recognizing the need to
reduce these benefits, Government issued a decree that reduces maximum sick leave entitlement to one
month per year and submitted the supporting legislation to the Majlisi Oli. Additionally, Government
plans to transfer responsibility for sickness and maternity leave benefits to the enterprise responsible for
employing the individual.
7.    The Employment Fund was set up to finance the Employment Centers -- the main institutions
through which certain benefits for labor are delivered, e.g., job placement, payment of unemployment
benefits, public works for the unemployed, training and retraining, protection of disabled and
disadvantaged workers, and registration and repatriation of refugees from the civil war. There are two
immediate problems with Employment Centers that need to be addressed. First, as presently constituted,
the unemployment funds are regional with the result if enterprises in a particular region do not pay the
wage bill tax, unemployment benefits are not paid. A more centralized fund would allow inter-regional
transfers to more distressed areas. Second, with the current unemployment benefits set equal to the
minimum wage and an employment tax of one percent, the Employment Fund would run a deficit if those
claiming benefits are more than four percent of the labor force. Therefore, Government has discontinued
financing wage subsidies for maintaining jobs in financially distressed enterprises.
SUPPLEMENTARY JOB-CREATION
8.    The combination of only very slow economic recovery (and therefore slow employment growth)
and a rapidly growing labor force (by at least 100,000 annually) mean the problem of unemployment will
not be solved by growth in the near term. Even if economic growth were to be as much as five percent
per year, in contrast to the projection of continuing decline for the next two to three years, the number
of new jobs would still be only about 60,000 per year -- well short of what is necessary to absorb new
entrants to the labor force.Recognizing the magnitude of the unemployment problem, Government has
allocated TR150 million for the public works program managed by the Employment Service. Such an
approach is especially attractive given the considerable amount of rehabilitation and reconstruction work
(e.g., roads, bridges, schools and clinics) that needs to be completed.
POVERTY ASSESSMENT
9.    The Government needs assistance to prepare a comprehensive poverty reduction strategy. This
would include preparing a profile of the poor and of vulnerable groups as well as mechanisms for
monitoring changes in poverty. Because of acute data limitations, technical support will be needed to
prepare this profile and the poverty reduction strategy. Under the Credit, agreement was reached with
the Government on the terms of reference for a poverty assessment.



- 105 -
ANNEX H
REPUBLIC OF TAJIKISTAN
PILOT POVERTY ALLEVIATION PROJECT
DRAFT GOVERNMENT RESOLUTION ESTABLISHING THE TASIF
1.    In accordance with the aim of realization of the Pilot Poverty Alleviation Project (PPAP) in the
Republic of Tajikistan, proposed and financed by the World Bank, which aims to solve social, economic,
and other problems of the more socially vulnerable populations, by means of creating additional
employment, rehabilitation of the most important social infrastructure works, implementation and
realization of microprojects defined by the local population, assistance to the population in adapting their
activities and skills to new conditions of the market economy, as well as by providing effective control
of the realization of the program implemented by NGOs within the Pilot Project and target used of credit
resources given, the Government of the Republic of Tajikistan decrees:
2.    To establish the Tajik Social Investment Fund, which is a non-commercial, independent, and
autonomous organization responsible for the implementation of microprojects, in the territory of the Tajik
Republic, within the PPAP proposed by the World Bank.
3.    To approve the attached Regulation concerning the Tajik Social Investment Fund.
4.    To regulate that:
(a) The TASIF's supreme leading body is a Board, which consists of an equal number of
representatives of the Government of Tajikistan and non-governmental organizations (NGOs).
The Chairman of the Board of TASIF is the Prime Minister of the Republic of Tajikistan.
(b) The TASIF Executive Committee, headed by the Executive Director of TASIF, is subject to
the Board, manages the operational activity of the TASIF. The TASIF's Executive Director
is to be chosen on a competitive basis, and is appointed by the Government of the Republic
of Tajikistan.
(c) Personnel, and other administrative expenses, are provided by resources of the PPAP
foreseen for these purposes.
4.    Ministries, institutions, and local executive authorities (Khukumat) must assist TASIF in its
activities, including preparation, selection and implementation of microprojects locally aimed to solve
poverty problems.
Chairman of the Government of Republic of Tajikistan



- 106-
REGULATION ON THE TAJIK SOCIAL INVESTMENT FUND
General Regulations
1.    Tajik Social Investment Fund (hereafter referred to as "TASIF") is a special humanitarian
organization realized under the Pilot Poverty Alleviation Project (hereafter referred to as "PPAP") in the
Republic of Tajikistan which has been financed by the World Bank aims to rehabilitate and develop the
most important social infrastructure works, generate additional employment, design and implement
microprojects, which are based on the participation of the population as well as to provide coordination
within the sphere of the PPAP, programs which are realized by international non-government
organizations (hereafter referred to as "NGOs").
2.     TASIF realizes its activity in accordance with present legislation of the republic of Tajikistan, all
international Agreements made, procedures of the World Bank, Operational Manual and present
Regulation.
3.     TASIF is a legal entity. It possesses separate property, acquires property and non-property rights,
can make on its behalf contracts and can take the part of the prosecutor and defendant in the Highest
economic court and arbitration court.
4.     TASIF is responsible for the obligations for regarding the property which belongs to it, and it
incurs penalties according to present legislation of the Republic of Tajikistan.
5.     TASIF has an independent payment balance, different kinds of accounts in banks of the Republic
of Tajikistan in rubles and foreign currency in accordance with existing legislation of the Republic of
Tajikistan.
6.     TASIF has its own stamps, offices, letter-head and title registered in certain order.
7.     The conditions of present Regulation retain their legal authorities with the period of TASIF
activity.
II. Title, location, aims and lezality of TASIF activity.
8.     The title of TASIF:
-    full title in Tajik:
abbreviation:
-    full title in Russian:
abbreviation
-    full title in English: Tajik Social Investment Fund, abbreviation TASIF
9.     Location of TASIF  Bokhtar st. 17, Dushanbe 734001, Republic of Tajikistan
10.   TASIF has right of a legal entity from the moment, when decision regarding TASIF establishment
was taken by the Government of the Republic of Tajikistan.



- 107-
11.    TASIF realizes its activity within the period of implementation of the PPAP.
III.    Aims and Tasks of TASIF
12.    TASIF has the following aims
-      to provide assistance in resolving the poverty problems through creation of additional
jobs and attraction of the most socially vulnerable groups of population to undertake
income generating activities in conditions of market economy;
-      to provide assistance in increasing the population's activity aimed at resolving local social
tasks and problems;
-      to provide creation, development and rehabilitation of local social infrastructure as a
means of improvement of living standards as well as to provide access for both urban and
rural poor populations to it;
-      stimulation of activity amongst local contractors in the development and rehabilitation of
local social infrastructure; and
-      provision of small credit which are socially targeted and which are managed by
individuals, families, dehkan farms, small enterprises and other legal entities, intended
to promote the development and extension of entrepreneurial activity.
13.    The main tasks of TASIF are:
-      rehabilitation of small social infrastructure works through financing of micro-projects;
-      provision of technical, consultative and practical assistance to local authorities and NGOs
in preparation and realization of microprojects
-      formation and development of working skills within conditions of the market economy
in local organization and private enterprises which are connected to the realization of
projects which have social targeting;
-      generation of employment by locating micro-projects amongst local construction
companies in order to assist them to fulfill micro-projects;
-      monitoring of NGOs contracts executed under TASIF programs;
-      provision of necessary information on TASIF 's activities to the Government of the
Republic of Tajikistan and the World Bank.



- 108-
IV. Sources of Formation of Financial Resources and Property of TASIF
14.    TASIF is the owner of property which belongs to it.
15.    Property of TASIF consists of the main and circulating resources as well as other property cost
of which is it' s own in an independent payment balance.
16.    The sources of formation of financial resources and property of TASIF can be the following:
- financial and material contributions given by the Government of the Republic of Tajikistan;
- financial and material contributions given by the multi-lateral and bilateral programs of the
TASIF's activities
- charitable contributions, gifts of citizens and juridical persons;
- financial contributions given by local and foreign NGOs;
-  grants or gifts provided by foreign governments;
- other sources which are not forbidden by the legislation of the Republic of Tajikistan.
17.    TASIF financial resources must be utilized in accordance with the Operational Manual as well
as conditions mentioned in credit and grant agreements.
V.    Rights of TASIF
18.   In order to achieve the aims mentioned in Chapter III of present Regulation, TASIF has the right
to:
-  exercise ownership usage and disposition independently by the full property rights secured
to them, regulated by law and in compliance with aims of its activity,
- make contracts, take other legal actions, and acquire property and person rights;
- independently organize current and perspective activity;
- open current, foreign and correspondent accounts in banks of the Republic of Tajikistan;
- accumulate financial and material-technical resources, to use and dispose of them in order to
achieve its aim and to carry out its tasks;
- conduct conferences, seminars and training on issues relative to activities of TASIF;
- carry out, according to established order, advertisement, publishing and other activities
connected to TASIF's activities and its local branches.
- finance rehabilitation of infrastructure works, disburse credits, conduct technical appraisal of
micro-projects, organize competitions of the awards of contracts and to control the process
of conducting all indicated activities;
- make agreements with individual and local organizations on issues relative to its jurisdiction.



- 109-
-  take the part of prosecutor and defendant in judaical institutions;
-  establish a Consultative Council composed of local specialists which will work on a voluntary
basis to work out recommendation concerning various problems which may arise in the
process of realization of TASIF's activities.
-  engage in other actions, which do not contradict its own aims and existing legislation.
VI.   Governing body and Development of TASIF Activities
19.   The TASIF's highest leading authority is the Board of TASIF (hereafter referred to as "Board").
The Chairman of the Board is the Prime Minister of the Republic of Tajikistan.
20.   The Board consists of an equal number or representatives of Government and non-government
organizations.
21.   The representatives of the Government to the Board are to be appointed and released by the Prime
Minister of the republic of Tajikistan. The NGO representatives are to be appointed by the Chairman
of the Board on their introduction. The members of the Board undertake their authority on a voluntary
basis.
22.   The jurisdiction of the Board includes:
-  definition of strategies of TASIF activities and control of their realization
-  approval of the Operational Manual, annual budget and current financial plans as well as
reports on their fulfillment
-  approval of annual credit program and report on its fulfillment;
-  approval of microproject financing in the amount of more than US$50,000
-  approval of resolutions regarding competition independent auditors invited to review TASIF's
financial activities and following approval of results of audit;
-  review and taking decisions regarding changes and additions to the TASIF Regulations and
to the Operational Manual;
- taking decisions concerning regional branches of the Fund in the territory of the Republic of
Tajikistan
-  approval of the management structure of the Fund;
-  approval and releasing of Board members;
-  other actions in compliance with the present Regulation.



- 110-
23.   The Board meeting is to be held quarterly. Special meetings are to be held according initiative
of the Chairman or majority of the members. A Board meeting is authorized if not less than 50% of the
Board members participate in the meeting. The Board's decisions to be taken by the majority of votes
of the Board members present. In case of an equal vote, the Chairman's vote will be decisive.
24.   The TASIF Executive body is an Executive Committee, headed by the Executive Director. The
Executive Committee staff includes:
-  Executive Director
- Heads of Departments, and
-  Legal Advisor.
25.   Jurisdiction of the Executive Committee includes:
-  realization of TASIF aims and tasks as defined by present regulation
-  targeted usage of resources for financing infrastructure rehabilitation and disbursement of
credit financing in programs of TASIF activities.
- taking decisions concerning allocation and of credit resources;
-  design and approval of Terms References;
-  approval of official instructions and terms and conditions of financing microprojects
according to the regions and definitions of terms to implement them;
-  to conduct technical appraisal of microprojects in order to define their characteristic and costs
and their following approval;
-  to conduct the selection process of microprojects on a competitive basis according to regions
and determine the sequence of their realization;
-  to conduct the competition define implementing agencies of microprojects in cooperation with
local authorities.
-  to control the realization of microprojects and targeted usage of credit with relative local
authorities
-  to present quarterly and annual reports concerning TASIF activities and control of the
realization of decisions taken on the basis of these reports;
-  to take decisions concerning attraction of additional resources to TASIF in order to fulfill its
aims and tasks.
-  design of management structure of Fund;
-  to conduct competitive selection of auditors and inspectors;
-  to organize training of TASIF personnel and representatives of local organizations and
-  resolution of other items not within the executive jurisdiction of the TASIF Board.
26.   The TASIF Executive Director manages all routine activities. The TASIF Executive Director is
to be selected on a competitive basis with a vote of non-objection of the WB, and appointed by the
Government of the Republic of Tajikistan.
27.   The jurisdiction of the Executive Director includes:
- presentation of TASIF to governmental and non-governmental organizations, enterprises and
institutions within and outside the Republic of Tajikistan,



- to sign contracts and to make legal actions on behalf of TASIF,
- selection and presentation of microprojects for approval of the Board and Executive
Committee,
- participation in TASIF Board meetings with the right of voice but no vote,
-  organization the realization of decisions of the Board and Executive Committee
- management of TASIF's activities, including financial, administrative, labor related and
others;
-  management of the activities of TASIF Executive Committee.
- selection and placement of personnel, conclusion and cancellation of employment contracts,
- to dispose of the property and resources of TASIF in accordance with its legislative
documents, to open accounts in banks, to issue warrants, to sign financial and economic
documents etc.
- to make proposals to the Board concerning structural changes in TASIF.
- to carry out other functions which are not within the jurisdiction of the Board or Executive
Committee and in compliance with the present Regulation.
28.   The Executive Director has a personal responsibility to carry out potential tasks in association
with TASIF and regulates the level of responsibility of Departmental Heads of TASIF.
VII.   Accountina and Reporting.
29.   Accounting, book-keeping and statistic report as well as reporting is to be conducted in
accordance with requirements of present legislation of the Republic of Tajikistan, Operational manual and
procedures of the World Bank. The TASIF executive Director is responsible for reliability of the reports
provided.
30.   The results of TASIF activities are to be reflected in quarterly and annual reports presented for
approval to TASIF Board.
31.   Financial and technical audit of TASIF is realized by independent auditors chosen by the Board,
when necessary.
32.   The financial year coincides with a calendar year.
VIII. Dispute Resolution
33.   All disputes arising between TASIF and individuals or other juridical persons are to be resolved
by the Executive Committee o r the TASIF's Board if both disputing parties agree. In all other cases
arising disputes shall be referred to juridical authorities of the Republic of Tajikistan in accordance with
existing legislation.
IX.   Suspension of TASIF Activities
34.   Reorganization (merging, unification, division, apportionment and transformation) of TASIF is
realized by decision of the Government of the Republic of Tajikistan. All property and non property
rights of TASIF transferred to authorized persons as a result of reorganization of TASIF.



- 112-
35.   TASIF can be liquidated by decision of the Government of Tajikistan. Liquidation is to be made
by the liquidation commission, which is created by the Government of the Republic of Tajikistan in
accordance with existing legislation.
X.    Final Resolutions
36.   If one of the Clauses of the present Regulation is ineffective that will not affect its other Clauses.
37.   Changes and additions to the TASIF Regulation are to be made by decision of the Government
of the Republic of Tajikistan.

DRAFT
OUTLINE
LEGAL STATUS AND STRUCTURE & ROLES OF BOARD AND OF EXECUTIVE
OFFICE
1.    LEGAL STATUS OF THE TASIF:
A.    The TASIF should be set up as an independently operating and disbursing institution
which reports to the Government through the office of the Prime Minister.
B.    A Presidential Decree should be issued asap to establish the TASIF and to establish its
two main bodies (the Board and the Executive Office) and its authorities in managing funds on
behalf of the Government of Tajikistan. This decree will need to be confirmed by Parliament asap
and not later than for loan effectiveness.
C.    The TASIF will develop a Constitutional Charter for the Board and a Manual of
Operations which will lay down the rules and regulations with which it operates and how it
identifies micro-projects and commits and disburses funds. These two documents will require no
objection of the World Bank. The Manual of Operations will require to be in an advanced draft
format as WB-Board condition.



-116-
2.    STRUCTURE OF THE TASIF:
A.    See organogram and staffing table attached.
B.    ROLE OF THE BOARD.
C.    See note attached.
D.    This is to elaborate on the notes referred to in #.5 above.
E.    The Board should develop in the first quarter of its existence a Constitutional Charter
which lays down its operating mechanisms and its role, functions and authorities.
F.    The board will probably meet on a quarterly basis for scheduled meetings. Extraordinary
meetings could be called: conditions should be defined. It is the Secretary of the Board, the
Executive Director who organizes the board meetings with the approval of the Chairman of the
Board (the Prime Minister).
G.    The board meetings will follow an agenda approved by the Chairman. This agenda will
have some permanent functions:
*  once a year, approve the annual investment program  (include. performance
indicators)
and the budget for the next year;
*  twice a year, approve quarterly audit reports on procedures and accountancy;
*  each quarter, approve the implementation schedule of the Executive Office;
*  each quarter, approve the program and relative budget revisions;
*  each quarter, approve the progress report of the Executive office, and approve the
Executive Summary of the Quarterly Report for reporting to the Government through
the Prime Minister.
H.    The different departments and support units of the Executive Office of the TASIF will
also include some specific items on the agenda scheduled throughout the year to balance the
activities of the different regular quarterly board meetings.
I.    It is clear that what is meant by TASIF Board approval means that the Board verifies
whether the Executive Office (EO) has implemented its daily management task in accordance with
the Manual of Operations (MO), and that its performance is in line with the performance
indicators. The TASIF EO will be submitted to a bi-annual audit which will verify whether the
EO has followed the procedures as outlined in the MO and that its accounts are in accordance
with WB-standards. These audits will produce a report on two quarters, which will be submitted
to the Board for their approval. These audit reports provide the guarantee that the EO is
performing according to its mandate.
J.    The Board can propose modifications to the procedures in the MO. Such modifications
are normal as situations can change and as the MO cannot predict all kinds of circumstances.
However, they require WB no-objection.



- 117-
K.    The Board can propose modifications to the Overall Investment Strategy and to the
Annual Investment Program, but these modifications require WB no-objection.
L.    A no-objection procedure by the WB requires typically between two to four months
because of the time required for the transmission of the information.
M.    The Board is in charge to hire and fire the Executive Director of the EO. In the MO there
is a section which describes the Staff Service Rules (SSR). The Board will have to follow the
rules as described in the SSR to be able to enact that authority.
N.    The Chairman of the Board will sign contracts over a minimum threshold on approval
of these contracts by the Board. Signing a contract of that nature will require WB no-objection
as well. It is clear that a micro-project which exceeds the threshold will take a longer
implementation schedule than normal micro-projects (which fall within the threshold).
4.    ROLE AND FUNCTIONS OF THE EXECUTIVE OFFICE:
A.    The Executive Office (EO) under the direction of the Executive Director (ED) is in
charge of the daily management of the TASIF under strict procedures as described in the MO.
B.    The EO is in charge of selecting the microprojects to be presented in the Quarterly
Implementation Schedules to the Board in respect of the criteria and procedures set forth in the
MO and of the Annual Investment Program (AIP).
C.    The ED is responsible to manage its program to achieve the goals and objectives set forth
in the AIP. This may require him to recruit consultants and to purchase goods. Within his budget
limitations, and acting as a good housefather, he is therefore responsible to sign contracts on
these issues, and to authorize and sign disbursement orders. The ED is only authorized to sign
contracts and authorize and sign disbursement orders within the threshold. He cannot sign
extensions or change orders to contracts which carry the original total contracts' amount above
that threshold.
D.    In order to be able to disburse the EO will have to open a bank account, at a commercial
banking institution of the ED's choice - with approval of the Board and no-objection of the WB.
E.    The ED will delegate the task of managing the personnel matters to the Finance and
Administration Manager (FAM). He will supervise that task. The FAM will ensure that the SSR
will be fully respected, and in that respect the FAM will organize - after the approval of next
year's program and budget - that all the staff will participate in the setting of the next year's
performance indicators for each of them, as well as evaluating each of the staff against the
previously set performance indicators. Consequently to this evaluation exercise the ED will make
a proposal to the next board meeting concerning staff bonuses, promotions and/or sanctions.
F.    The ED will delegate the task of the preparation of the Annual Investment Program (with
eventual revision of the Global Investment Strategy) to the Investment Planner (IP). The IP will
organize through consultants a special targeting exercise, to identify the highest poverty areas in



- 118 -
the country, in the regions and in the districts with comparative poverty assessment methods. The
targeting is an important exercise to ensure that the objectives of the TASIF are really being met.
G.    The ED will delegate to the Micro-Project Area Managers the task of the promotion, the
identification, the selection, the preparation, the implementation and supervision and the hand-
over of the micro-projects in accordance with the procedures of the MO.
H.    The MP1&2 will further organize through their promotion unit another targeting exercise
(through consultants) which consists in identifying the highest poverty communities within the
highest priority poverty districts. The consultants will then actively promote the project in those
highest priority communities. In the process of promotion, the consultant will also provide
information on how to lower or defy harassment.
I.     The MP1&2 will ensure that micro-projects will be selected in accordance of the
procedures and criteria as described in the MO:
J.     The MP1&2 will ensure that the communities will be actively involved in the entire
process cycle of the micro-projects, from the identification, through the preparation to the
implementation, handover and operation and maintenance of it. Several options degrees of
participation of communities are available to ensure both that the micro-project responds to the
communities' highest needs and that through their participation a sense of ownership develops
which is a large part of the sustainability of the micro-project. Wherever the community lacks
the skills in the micro-project cycle the TASIF can involve consultants.
K.    The communities will participate for approx. 15% to the cost of the micro-project. As
this is indeed a heavy contribution from these poorest communities, a very wide variety of
possibilities should be explored to achieve this goal. Besides financial, labor and or material
contributions other solutions should be acceptable to TASIF, even if this may lead to some un-
desirable side activities.
L.    The micro-projects will need, to be environmentally sound. They should certainly have
no negative effect on the environment, and preferably improve the situation. Sensitive micro-
projects are water and waste water related, surface drainages which can cause erosion, and other
types of micro-projects.
M.    The micro-projects should be cost-effective. This means that an effort has to be put in
to design technical specifications which are less costly, and that a competitive procurement
procedure has to be undertaken. Cost efficiency of scale is not a priority. But it is also important
to ensure that the final quality of the works will be of the best available standards.
N.    The micro-projects should be sustainable. The MP1&2 should ensure that a maintenance
and operations plan is being designed for the output of the micro-project which includes
identification of budgets and how this budgets will be obtained. Solid guarantees for this are
required before approval of the micro-project. If community contributions are required, a cost
recovery mechanism has to be designed and assurances have to be sought that they will be applied
once the micro-project is handed-over to the community or the client.



- 119-
0.    The MP1&2 will ensure that proper supervision will be installed on each of the micro-
projects under implementation. Local supervisors - eventually proposed by the communities - are
preferable. Strict supervision reporting and consequent progress payment procedures will be
installed to enter into the computerized monitoring system of the TASIF.
P.    The ED will ensure, with the assistance of the procurement specialist that all procurement
procedures in the TASIF will be in accordance with WB rules and regulations and with the
specific details as stated in the MO.
Q.    The ED will ensure that the MIS Manager keeps up to date a complex and detailed
Management Information System (MIS) which gathers data on processes and progress for the use
of the different managers in the EO. The MIS is a most important tool for managing this type
of projects. Although a technologically simple project, the management of multiple small funds
delegated to inexperienced and widely dispersed organizations within a country with poor
communication means is a high risk undertaking. A very thorough collection of data will have
to be put in place, with strict reporting procedures and an MIS system which can provide very
up-to-date globalized reporting for the managers. It is important that the managers instill
themselves the discipline to make optimal use of the outputs of the MIS: they are the example
to the lower staff and to the NGO's and communities, and they need the information to ensure
that the project is well managed and can generate the kind of quantities of micro-projects which
can have an impact on the poverty.
R.    The ED will delegate the task of keeping very accurate accounts to the FAM. The FAM
will receive documented justifications for each commitments and expenditures from the MIS
system. Commitments and expenditures without such justification cannot be entered into the
accountancy system. The MIS and the accountancy system will work in parallel, but as two
independent mechanisms. The design of both should allow for easy comparison between them.
S.    The ED will facilitate the regular audits over the TASIF. Bi-annual audits will be
conducted to control the respect of the procedures and the financial rules and regulations of the
project. The audits will be conducted over two quarters of the year, and should produce a report
which can be presented to the board within three months after the end of the second quarter
covered by the audit. This auditing procedure guarantees that the EO cannot abuse the authorities
of micro-project selection, contract signing and disbursement vested in its autonomous status. An
annual audit, consolidation of two bi-annual audits will also be produced.
T.    The ED will produce a commentary to the bi-annual audit to the same board meeting,
certainly when the audits point out irregularities. The ED should organize a competitive bidding
to allow the board to appoint the audits.
U.    The EO will conduct regular impact evaluation exercises, which consist in measuring the
impact of the TASIF program versus its objectives. Indicators will be developed for that purpose.
The EO will study these impact evaluations very carefully and prepare recommendations how
impact can be improved and/or how impact evaluation can be improved. The WB will conduct
impact evaluations over the project as well, and compare notes with the internal impact evaluation
reports.



- 120-
ANNEX J
REPUBLIC OF TAJIKISTAN
PILOT POVERTY ALLEVIATION PROJECT
INSTITUTIONAL ORGANIZATION OF TASIF
Management Information System Specialist
Consultant to the Tajikistan Social Investnent Fund
Draft Terms of Reference
1.    The Government of Tajikistan will establish the Tajikistan Social Investment Fund
(TASIF) as a mechanism to reduce poverty through the financing of labor-intensive works and
other income-generating microprojects identified and implemented by community-based
organizations. Small private building contractors will be selected competitively to execute
contracts whenever feasible and Non-governmental Organizations (NGOs) will be used to target
poorer segments of the population who have potential to benefit from small income-generation
projects, especially in agriculture production and marketing.
2.    A computerized Management Information System (MIS) is needed to track the large
number of microprojects to be financed by the TASIF. The MIS must be interactive so that
TASIF staff can input information on a day-to-day basis, while also being designed with adequate
security measures. The attributes of the MIS will include the ability to:
o         store basic information on microprojects;
*         track the microproject portfolio through the microproject cycle;
*         record materials and inputs needed for each microproject; and
*         track financial disbursements.
3.    The MIS will enable simplified reports to be created for managers of the TASIF to
facilitate their day-to-day management and to meet reporting requirements of the TASIF Board
and donors participating in the project.
4.    The MIS Specialist will provide technical assistance to the MIS Officer of the TASIF in
order to conceptualize and develop an MIS for the TASIF that meets World Bank specifications
for project effectiveness. The MIS Specialist will be responsible for:



- 121 -
5.    Assessing the information needs of the TASIF, taking into account its administrative and
organizational structure and reporting requirements
6.    Work with the TASIF MIS Officer to conceptualize and develop an MIS for the TASIF
by either adopting an existing system or creating a new one. This is to be done within reasonable
financial boundaries and with cognizance of available local skills and support systems needed to
operate and maintain an MIS in Tajikistan.
7.    Providing specifications on the hardware and software to be procured for the MIS.
8.    Providing guidelines to TASIF on the skills and qualifications needed to maintain the
system.
9.    Advising the MIS Officer who will be responsible for training TASIF staff in operating
and maintaining the system.
10.   Time-frame: It is estimated that the consultant would travel to Tajikistan in December-
January for approximately 2 weeks. This would be followed up by 2-3 times over the subsequent
12 months to guide development, testing and refinement of the MIS.
11.   Qualifications: The consultant will have a strong background in database development
maintenance and be familiar with MIS systems used in similar projects, and software to run such
systems. The consultant will also be experienced in conceptualizing, developing and operating
computerized integrated management information and accounting systems. The consultant will
speak Russian. The best qualified consultant will be experienced in developing and upgrading an
MIS for other social funds.
